## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard form of kinetic rate laws for well-mixed (0D) chemical reactors. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are autonomous or time-varying rate laws where the reaction rate depends on concentration (mass-action) and possibly explicit time dependence (e.g., catalyst deactivation, programmed temperature).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption, e.g., surface-limited or saturated regime)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition limit)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with other reactant in excess absorbed into c0)
- General n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating until depletion/limit)
- Reversible first-order to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible nonlinear to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A**c1 - c2) (drives A toward an equilibrium defined in transformed coordinates)
- Parallel loss channels (linear + nonlinear): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (two mechanisms active simultaneously)
- Inhibition / crowding-limited rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective rate reduced at high A)
- Time-dependent first-order (programmed conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant drifts linearly with time)
- Exponential deactivation of activity: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (rate slows due to catalyst deactivation or cooling schedule)
- Periodic forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated conditions such as light chopping)
- Source/sink with baseline feed or leak: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (net production c0 with first-order removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action signature: if dA_dt scales like A, A**2, or A**n, it indicates unimolecular/bimolecular/overall-order kinetics.
- Irreversible consumption constraint: for a decaying reactant in a closed batch system, dA_dt should be nonpositive for A > 0; models like -c0*A**c1 naturally enforce this.
- Equilibrium relaxation: presence of (A - c1) (or similar) implies asymptotic approach to a nonzero steady state A -> c1.
- Multiple mechanisms: sums of terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) suggest parallel pathways or mixed control regimes across concentration ranges.
- Inhibition/crowding: rational forms like A/(1+c*A) encode diminishing marginal rate at high concentration (effective rate constant decreases with A).
- Time-varying conditions: explicit t factors multiplying A (e.g., exp(-c*t)*A, (1+c*t)*A) indicate changing temperature, catalyst activity, illumination, or mixing over time.
- Externally forced kinetics: sinusoidal dependence on t points to periodic operation (light modulation, oscillatory temperature control), often producing non-exponential A(t).
- Baseline source term: an additive +c0 in dA_dt implies feed/generation independent of A (leak-in, zeroth-order formation) competing with removal.
